Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Infallibility: A Condition for Prophets, Not Imams
Al-Nasafi asserts that infallibility is not required for the imam because it is a condition for prophethood, proven by miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that infallibility is a condition exclusive to prophets and not required for the imam.

Core Idea
Infallibility is proven by miracles, and imams have no miracles.

Al-Nasafi begins by distinguishing between the imam and the prophet. While the prophet is chosen directly by God and supported by miracles that prove his infallibility, the imam is elected by the community and does not possess such miraculous proofs. Therefore, infallibility cannot be a condition for the imam.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening contrast
Read the passage where al-Nasafi contrasts the imam with the prophet. Note how the prophet's infallibility is tied to miracles.
The prophet is chosen by God, the imam by people.
2
Identify the core premise
The author states that infallibility is a condition of prophethood because it is accompanied by signs and miracles.
Miracles are beyond normal customs.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since imams lack miracles, they cannot have infallibility as a condition.
The imam's role is different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتعليق الحكم به فائدة بخلاف النبوة، فإن الله تعالى هو الذي يختار من يشاء من عباده لرسالته ونبوته، وهو العالم بحقيقة كل شيء، فكان من اختاره من أهل زمانه لرسالته وتحميل أمانته أفضل خليقته وأكمل بريته في وقته، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله تعالى الموفق

لا يشترط عصمة الإمام لأن العصمة للأنبياء وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا بل العصمة من شرط النبوة إذ هي مقترنة بأعلام، ومعجزات خارجات عن العادات والطبائع يعرف بذلك صدقهم وتظهر عصمتهم، وليس الأئمة شيء من ذلك، فلو وجب القول بعصمته لوجب مع من غير دليل، إذ لا عصمة بدون صحة السريرة وسلامة الباطن، ولا وقوف على ذلك إلا بالوحي، ولا وحي مع من يختار الإمام لعقد الإمامة وهم مأمورون بنصب الإمام على ما بينا، فلو لزمهم نصب الإمام المعصوم وليس معهم دليل عصمته فكان فيه تكليف ما ليس في الوسع، والله تعالى تبرأ عن تكليف مثله بقوله تعالى: { لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا } إِلَّا مَا ءَاتَنها وغير ذلك، وقبح ذلك أيضا في العقول، على أن النبي عليه السلام يأتي بما هو غائب عن أهل الأرض، وهو الشريعة التي أتى بها وبه ظهور ذلك، ثم يظهر ذلك فيهم بالقول تارة وبالفعل أخرى، فلو لم يكن معصوما لكذب في تبليغه أو نسق في تعاطيه، فتقبل الناس قوله بإباحة شيء هو محرم في الحقيقة إلا أنه كاذب في تبليغه إباحته، وكذا اعتقدوا إباحة ما عاينوه يتعاطى بناء للأمر على رسالته الثابتة بإعلامه ومعجزاته وذلك في الحقيقة محظور لا مباح فيقع في الناس في الضلال، واعتقاد إباحة ما هو حرام بناء للأمر على المعجزات فتكون المعجزة التي أقامها الله تعالى حجة للرسول موقعة للناس في الكفر والضلال فلابد من ثبوت العصمة لرسول لئلا يؤدي إلى ذلك المحال.

فأما الأئمة فما جاءوا بأمر غائب عن أهل الأرض بل هم أمروا بالعمل بما جاء به الرسول عليه السلام من القرآن وغيره، وذلك ظاهر فيما بين الناس، وقد قام بمعرفة ذلك كله علماء الأمة وإنما الإمام للعمل بذلك والحكم به فيما بين الخلق وهو كسائر الأمة في العمل بذلك يظهر صوابه وخطأه بما به يظهر صواب غيره وخطأه، فلا معنى لاشتراط عصمته، وقد بينا بطلان القول بعصمة الإمام في كتابنا المصنف في الرد على الباطنية المترجم بكتاب الإفساد لخدع أهل الإلحاد - بما فيه كفاية وفيما ذكرنا لها هنا مقنع.
It has benefit to attach the ruling to him unlike prophethood, for God Almighty is the one who chooses whom He wills from His servants for His message and prophethood, and He is the Knower of the reality of everything. So the one He chose from the people of his time for His message and the burden of His trust was the best of His creation and the most complete of His creatures in his time, while in the matter we are discussing, the opposite is the case, and God Almighty is the Grantor of success.

Infallibility of the imam is not a condition because infallibility is for the prophets. Likewise, his being infallible is not a condition according to us; rather, infallibility is a condition of prophethood since it is accompanied by signs and miracles that go beyond customs and natures, by which their truthfulness is known and their infallibility appears. The imams have nothing of that. So if the claim of his infallibility were obligatory, it would be obligatory without evidence, for there is no infallibility without soundness of the inner self and purity of the inner state, and there is no knowledge of that except through revelation, and there is no revelation with those who choose the imam for the contract of imamah, while they are commanded to appoint the imam as we explained. So if they were required to appoint an infallible imam while they have no evidence of his infallibility, that would involve a burden beyond capacity, and God Almighty absolved Himself from such a burden by His saying: {God does not burden a soul except its capacity} except what it has been given, and other verses. That is also considered ugly in the intellects. Moreover, the Prophet, peace be upon him, brings what is unseen to the people of the earth, namely the Sharia he brought, and by him its appearance occurs, then he manifests it among them sometimes by word and sometimes by deed. If he were not infallible, he would lie in his conveyance or err in his practice, then the people would accept his saying that something is permissible while it is actually forbidden, except that he is lying in conveying its permissibility, and similarly they would believe the permissibility of what they see him practicing based on his confirmed message with signs and miracles, while that is in reality prohibited, not permissible. So they would fall into error, and believing the permissibility of what is forbidden based on miracles would cause the miracle that God established as a proof for the messenger to lead people into unbelief and error. Therefore, the establishment of infallibility for a messenger is necessary lest that impossible consequence occur.

As for the imams, they did not bring any matter unseen to the people of the earth; rather, they are commanded to act according to what the Messenger, peace be upon him, brought from the Quran and other things, and that is apparent among the people. The scholars of the community have the knowledge of all that, and the imam is only for acting upon that and judging by it among the creation, and he is like the rest of the community in acting upon that; his correctness and error are revealed by that which reveals the correctness and error of others. So there is no meaning to stipulating his infallibility. We have already demonstrated the invalidity of the claim of the imam's infallibility in our book composed in refutation of the Batiniyya, entitled 'The Book of Corruption of the Deceptions of the People of Atheism' - that is sufficient, and what we have mentioned here is convincing.
Source pages p. 1121

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the condition of infallibility (عصمة) for the imam. The author begins by contrasting the imam with the prophet: the prophet is chosen by God and brings a new divine law, so his infallibility is necessary to prevent leading people into error. The imam, however, does not bring a new law but only applies the existing law. The author then states that infallibility is not a condition for the imam because it is only a condition for prophethood, which is proven by miracles and signs. Since the imam lacks such signs, requiring infallibility would be an impossible obligation (تكليف ما ليس في الوسع), as there is no way to know a person's inner state except through revelation, and the imam is not appointed by revelation. The author supports this with a Quranic verse (2:286) and rational argument. He then explains why the prophet must be infallible: to avoid the contradiction of a miracle leading people to accept something false. Finally, he reiterates that the imam is merely a judge and executor of the law, and his errors are detectable by scholars, so infallibility is not needed.

Key Terms
عصمة
إمام
نبوة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that the imam must be infallible because he is a religious leader.
Correction: Al-Nasafi clarifies that infallibility is only known through miracles and divine choice, which apply to prophets, not to imams who are elected by people.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why is infallibility not a condition for the imam?
A) Because the imam is not as important as a prophet
B) Because infallibility is tied to miracles which imams lack
C) Because all Muslims are fallible
D) Because the imam is chosen by the people

Key Takeaway
Infallibility is a condition for prophets proven by miracles, not for imams who are chosen by the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever expect your religious leaders or teachers to be infallible? Where does that expectation come from, and how does this lesson challenge you to reconsider it? What will you do the next time you see a mistake in someone you follow?
?
If infallibility is only for prophets, then you are responsible for your own growth in knowledge and practice. Are you relying too heavily on others to tell you right from wrong without engaging with the sources yourself? How will you take ownership of your faith starting today?
?
This lesson teaches that prophets are proven by miracles and are sinless. Have you ever doubted the sinlessness of a prophet because of a story you heard? How does this passage strengthen your belief? What step will you take to learn more about the proofs of prophethood?

The Impossible Burden of Requiring an Infallible Imam
Al-Nasafi argues that requiring infallibility for the imam is an impossible obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's argument that requiring infallibility for the imam would impose an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yutiq).

Core Idea
Requiring infallibility without evidence is an impossible burden that God does not impose.

Al-Nasafi now presents a rational and scriptural argument against the condition of infallibility. He argues that since infallibility can only be known through revelation, and the imam is not appointed by revelation, requiring the community to select an infallible imam would be a burden beyond capacity. This is supported by the Quranic verse 'God does not burden a soul except its capacity'.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the passage carefully. Note the logical steps: infallibility requires knowledge of the inner self, which is only known through revelation.
2
Identify the burden
The author says that requiring people to appoint an infallible imam without evidence is 'taklif ma la yutiq' (a burden beyond capacity).
3
Connect to Quranic proof
He cites the verse 2:286 to show that God does not impose such a burden.
4
Rational argument
He also says that this would be considered ugly in the intellects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتعليق الحكم به فائدة بخلاف النبوة، فإن الله تعالى هو الذي يختار من يشاء من عباده لرسالته ونبوته، وهو العالم بحقيقة كل شيء، فكان من اختاره من أهل زمانه لرسالته وتحميل أمانته أفضل خليقته وأكمل بريته في وقته، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله تعالى الموفق

لا يشترط عصمة الإمام لأن العصمة للأنبياء وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا بل العصمة من شرط النبوة إذ هي مقترنة بأعلام، ومعجزات خارجات عن العادات والطبائع يعرف بذلك صدقهم وتظهر عصمتهم، وليس الأئمة شيء من ذلك، فلو وجب القول بعصمته لوجب مع من غير دليل، إذ لا عصمة بدون صحة السريرة وسلامة الباطن، ولا وقوف على ذلك إلا بالوحي، ولا وحي مع من يختار الإمام لعقد الإمامة وهم مأمورون بنصب الإمام على ما بينا، فلو لزمهم نصب الإمام المعصوم وليس معهم دليل عصمته فكان فيه تكليف ما ليس في الوسع، والله تعالى تبرأ عن تكليف مثله بقوله تعالى: { لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا } إِلَّا مَا ءَاتَنها وغير ذلك، وقبح ذلك أيضا في العقول، على أن النبي عليه السلام يأتي بما هو غائب عن أهل الأرض، وهو الشريعة التي أتى بها وبه ظهور ذلك، ثم يظهر ذلك فيهم بالقول تارة وبالفعل أخرى، فلو لم يكن معصوما لكذب في تبليغه أو نسق في تعاطيه، فتقبل الناس قوله بإباحة شيء هو محرم في الحقيقة إلا أنه كاذب في تبليغه إباحته، وكذا اعتقدوا إباحة ما عاينوه يتعاطى بناء للأمر على رسالته الثابتة بإعلامه ومعجزاته وذلك في الحقيقة محظور لا مباح فيقع في الناس في الضلال، واعتقاد إباحة ما هو حرام بناء للأمر على المعجزات فتكون المعجزة التي أقامها الله تعالى حجة للرسول موقعة للناس في الكفر والضلال فلابد من ثبوت العصمة لرسول لئلا يؤدي إلى ذلك المحال.

فأما الأئمة فما جاءوا بأمر غائب عن أهل الأرض بل هم أمروا بالعمل بما جاء به الرسول عليه السلام من القرآن وغيره، وذلك ظاهر فيما بين الناس، وقد قام بمعرفة ذلك كله علماء الأمة وإنما الإمام للعمل بذلك والحكم به فيما بين الخلق وهو كسائر الأمة في العمل بذلك يظهر صوابه وخطأه بما به يظهر صواب غيره وخطأه، فلا معنى لاشتراط عصمته، وقد بينا بطلان القول بعصمة الإمام في كتابنا المصنف في الرد على الباطنية المترجم بكتاب الإفساد لخدع أهل الإلحاد - بما فيه كفاية وفيما ذكرنا لها هنا مقنع.
It has benefit to attach the ruling to him unlike prophethood, for God Almighty is the one who chooses whom He wills from His servants for His message and prophethood, and He is the Knower of the reality of everything. So the one He chose from the people of his time for His message and the burden of His trust was the best of His creation and the most complete of His creatures in his time, while in the matter we are discussing, the opposite is the case, and God Almighty is the Grantor of success.

Infallibility of the imam is not a condition because infallibility is for the prophets. Likewise, his being infallible is not a condition according to us; rather, infallibility is a condition of prophethood since it is accompanied by signs and miracles that go beyond customs and natures, by which their truthfulness is known and their infallibility appears. The imams have nothing of that. So if the claim of his infallibility were obligatory, it would be obligatory without evidence, for there is no infallibility without soundness of the inner self and purity of the inner state, and there is no knowledge of that except through revelation, and there is no revelation with those who choose the imam for the contract of imamah, while they are commanded to appoint the imam as we explained. So if they were required to appoint an infallible imam while they have no evidence of his infallibility, that would involve a burden beyond capacity, and God Almighty absolved Himself from such a burden by His saying: {God does not burden a soul except its capacity} except what it has been given, and other verses. That is also considered ugly in the intellects. Moreover, the Prophet, peace be upon him, brings what is unseen to the people of the earth, namely the Sharia he brought, and by him its appearance occurs, then he manifests it among them sometimes by word and sometimes by deed. If he were not infallible, he would lie in his conveyance or err in his practice, then the people would accept his saying that something is permissible while it is actually forbidden, except that he is lying in conveying its permissibility, and similarly they would believe the permissibility of what they see him practicing based on his confirmed message with signs and miracles, while that is in reality prohibited, not permissible. So they would fall into error, and believing the permissibility of what is forbidden based on miracles would cause the miracle that God established as a proof for the messenger to lead people into unbelief and error. Therefore, the establishment of infallibility for a messenger is necessary lest that impossible consequence occur.

As for the imams, they did not bring any matter unseen to the people of the earth; rather, they are commanded to act according to what the Messenger, peace be upon him, brought from the Quran and other things, and that is apparent among the people. The scholars of the community have the knowledge of all that, and the imam is only for acting upon that and judging by it among the creation, and he is like the rest of the community in acting upon that; his correctness and error are revealed by that which reveals the correctness and error of others. So there is no meaning to stipulating his infallibility. We have already demonstrated the invalidity of the claim of the imam's infallibility in our book composed in refutation of the Batiniyya, entitled 'The Book of Corruption of the Deceptions of the People of Atheism' - that is sufficient, and what we have mentioned here is convincing.
Source pages p. 1121

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the condition of infallibility (عصمة) for the imam. The author begins by contrasting the imam with the prophet: the prophet is chosen by God and brings a new divine law, so his infallibility is necessary to prevent leading people into error. The imam, however, does not bring a new law but only applies the existing law. The author then states that infallibility is not a condition for the imam because it is only a condition for prophethood, which is proven by miracles and signs. Since the imam lacks such signs, requiring infallibility would be an impossible obligation (تكليف ما ليس في الوسع), as there is no way to know a person's inner state except through revelation, and the imam is not appointed by revelation. The author supports this with a Quranic verse (2:286) and rational argument. He then explains why the prophet must be infallible: to avoid the contradiction of a miracle leading people to accept something false. Finally, he reiterates that the imam is merely a judge and executor of the law, and his errors are detectable by scholars, so infallibility is not needed.

C) It would be a condition for prophethood
D) It would be proven by miracles

Key Takeaway
Requiring infallibility for the imam would impose an impossible obligation that contradicts divine justice and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever insisted on a religious view without clear evidence, and then felt the burden of convincing others? How does Al-Nasafi's argument call you to humility and trust in revelation?
?
God does not burden you beyond capacity—but are you burdening yourself with expectations that are not from Him? What would change if you accepted that some things are known only through revelation and not your own efforts?

Why Prophets Must Be Infallible
Al-Nasafi demonstrates the necessity of prophetic infallibility to avoid contradiction with miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's argument that prophets must be infallible to prevent miracles from leading people into error.

Core Idea
If prophets were not infallible, their miracles could lead people to accept falsehood.

After arguing against infallibility for the imam, al-Nasafi explains why prophets must be infallible. He uses a hypothetical scenario: if a prophet were to lie or err, his miracles would cause people to believe falsehood, which would be a contradiction of the miracle's purpose. Therefore, infallibility is necessary for prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophetic scenario
Read the passage about the prophet bringing unseen Sharia. Note the role of miracles.
2
Identify the dangerous consequence
If the prophet were not infallible, his actions could lead people to accept forbidden things as permissible.
3
Understand the logical necessity
Miracles are proofs of truthfulness; if a prophet erred, the miracle would become a cause of error, which is impossible.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a single error from a prophet could lead people to eternal loss, how seriously do you take the task of conveying the truth to others? Will you commit to studying the proofs of prophethood so that you can confidently defend the infallibility of the Messenger?
?
The argument shows that God would not allow His miracles to endorse falsehood. When you accept a religious ruling, do you verify that it comes from an infallible source? Or do you sometimes follow your desires, trusting in your own reasoning? How will you ensure your practice aligns with what the Prophet actually taught?
?
Consider that the very miracles that prove prophethood would, without infallibility, become a means of misguidance. In your own life, are there blessings or signs from God that you have turned into excuses for sin? What will you do to ensure that God’s favors lead you closer to Him, not away?

The Imam's Role Does Not Require Infallibility
Al-Nasafi concludes that the imam's function does not necessitate infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's concluding argument that the imam merely applies the existing law, so infallibility is unnecessary.

Core Idea
The imam only judges by the revealed law, which is already known; infallibility is not needed.

Al-Nasafi concludes by directly addressing the imam's function. Unlike the prophet who brings new law, the imam only enforces the law already revealed. The scholars are the ones who preserve and know the law, and the imam is simply a judge. His errors can be detected by others, so infallibility is not a condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the imam's function
Notice that the imam does not bring anything unseen; he only acts based on the Quran and Sunnah.
2
Understand the role of scholars
The scholars know the law, so the imam is not the sole authority.
3
See the contrast with prophets
The prophet's role required infallibility; the imam's does not.
4
Note the author's reference to his book
He says he already refuted the Batiniyya on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتعليق الحكم به فائدة بخلاف النبوة، فإن الله تعالى هو الذي يختار من يشاء من عباده لرسالته ونبوته، وهو العالم بحقيقة كل شيء، فكان من اختاره من أهل زمانه لرسالته وتحميل أمانته أفضل خليقته وأكمل بريته في وقته، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله تعالى الموفق

لا يشترط عصمة الإمام لأن العصمة للأنبياء وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا بل العصمة من شرط النبوة إذ هي مقترنة بأعلام، ومعجزات خارجات عن العادات والطبائع يعرف بذلك صدقهم وتظهر عصمتهم، وليس الأئمة شيء من ذلك، فلو وجب القول بعصمته لوجب مع من غير دليل، إذ لا عصمة بدون صحة السريرة وسلامة الباطن، ولا وقوف على ذلك إلا بالوحي، ولا وحي مع من يختار الإمام لعقد الإمامة وهم مأمورون بنصب الإمام على ما بينا، فلو لزمهم نصب الإمام المعصوم وليس معهم دليل عصمته فكان فيه تكليف ما ليس في الوسع، والله تعالى تبرأ عن تكليف مثله بقوله تعالى: { لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا } إِلَّا مَا ءَاتَنها وغير ذلك، وقبح ذلك أيضا في العقول، على أن النبي عليه السلام يأتي بما هو غائب عن أهل الأرض، وهو الشريعة التي أتى بها وبه ظهور ذلك، ثم يظهر ذلك فيهم بالقول تارة وبالفعل أخرى، فلو لم يكن معصوما لكذب في تبليغه أو نسق في تعاطيه، فتقبل الناس قوله بإباحة شيء هو محرم في الحقيقة إلا أنه كاذب في تبليغه إباحته، وكذا اعتقدوا إباحة ما عاينوه يتعاطى بناء للأمر على رسالته الثابتة بإعلامه ومعجزاته وذلك في الحقيقة محظور لا مباح فيقع في الناس في الضلال، واعتقاد إباحة ما هو حرام بناء للأمر على المعجزات فتكون المعجزة التي أقامها الله تعالى حجة للرسول موقعة للناس في الكفر والضلال فلابد من ثبوت العصمة لرسول لئلا يؤدي إلى ذلك المحال.

فأما الأئمة فما جاءوا بأمر غائب عن أهل الأرض بل هم أمروا بالعمل بما جاء به الرسول عليه السلام من القرآن وغيره، وذلك ظاهر فيما بين الناس، وقد قام بمعرفة ذلك كله علماء الأمة وإنما الإمام للعمل بذلك والحكم به فيما بين الخلق وهو كسائر الأمة في العمل بذلك يظهر صوابه وخطأه بما به يظهر صواب غيره وخطأه، فلا معنى لاشتراط عصمته، وقد بينا بطلان القول بعصمة الإمام في كتابنا المصنف في الرد على الباطنية المترجم بكتاب الإفساد لخدع أهل الإلحاد - بما فيه كفاية وفيما ذكرنا لها هنا مقنع.
It has benefit to attach the ruling to him unlike prophethood, for God Almighty is the one who chooses whom He wills from His servants for His message and prophethood, and He is the Knower of the reality of everything. So the one He chose from the people of his time for His message and the burden of His trust was the best of His creation and the most complete of His creatures in his time, while in the matter we are discussing, the opposite is the case, and God Almighty is the Grantor of success.

Infallibility of the imam is not a condition because infallibility is for the prophets. Likewise, his being infallible is not a condition according to us; rather, infallibility is a condition of prophethood since it is accompanied by signs and miracles that go beyond customs and natures, by which their truthfulness is known and their infallibility appears. The imams have nothing of that. So if the claim of his infallibility were obligatory, it would be obligatory without evidence, for there is no infallibility without soundness of the inner self and purity of the inner state, and there is no knowledge of that except through revelation, and there is no revelation with those who choose the imam for the contract of imamah, while they are commanded to appoint the imam as we explained. So if they were required to appoint an infallible imam while they have no evidence of his infallibility, that would involve a burden beyond capacity, and God Almighty absolved Himself from such a burden by His saying: {God does not burden a soul except its capacity} except what it has been given, and other verses. That is also considered ugly in the intellects. Moreover, the Prophet, peace be upon him, brings what is unseen to the people of the earth, namely the Sharia he brought, and by him its appearance occurs, then he manifests it among them sometimes by word and sometimes by deed. If he were not infallible, he would lie in his conveyance or err in his practice, then the people would accept his saying that something is permissible while it is actually forbidden, except that he is lying in conveying its permissibility, and similarly they would believe the permissibility of what they see him practicing based on his confirmed message with signs and miracles, while that is in reality prohibited, not permissible. So they would fall into error, and believing the permissibility of what is forbidden based on miracles would cause the miracle that God established as a proof for the messenger to lead people into unbelief and error. Therefore, the establishment of infallibility for a messenger is necessary lest that impossible consequence occur.

As for the imams, they did not bring any matter unseen to the people of the earth; rather, they are commanded to act according to what the Messenger, peace be upon him, brought from the Quran and other things, and that is apparent among the people. The scholars of the community have the knowledge of all that, and the imam is only for acting upon that and judging by it among the creation, and he is like the rest of the community in acting upon that; his correctness and error are revealed by that which reveals the correctness and error of others. So there is no meaning to stipulating his infallibility. We have already demonstrated the invalidity of the claim of the imam's infallibility in our book composed in refutation of the Batiniyya, entitled 'The Book of Corruption of the Deceptions of the People of Atheism' - that is sufficient, and what we have mentioned here is convincing.
Source pages p. 1121

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the condition of infallibility (عصمة) for the imam. The author begins by contrasting the imam with the prophet: the prophet is chosen by God and brings a new divine law, so his infallibility is necessary to prevent leading people into error. The imam, however, does not bring a new law but only applies the existing law. The author then states that infallibility is not a condition for the imam because it is only a condition for prophethood, which is proven by miracles and signs. Since the imam lacks such signs, requiring infallibility would be an impossible obligation (تكليف ما ليس في الوسع), as there is no way to know a person's inner state except through revelation, and the imam is not appointed by revelation. The author supports this with a Quranic verse (2:286) and rational argument. He then explains why the prophet must be infallible: to avoid the contradiction of a miracle leading people to accept something false. Finally, he reiterates that the imam is merely a judge and executor of the law, and his errors are detectable by scholars, so infallibility is not needed.

Key Terms
إمام
شريعة
علماء
حكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the role of the imam according to al-Nasafi?
A) To bring new divine law
B) To act and judge based on the known Sharia
C) To perform miracles
D) To be infallible like prophets

Key Takeaway
The imam's role as an implementer of existing law does not require infallibility, unlike the prophet's role as a lawgiver.

Imamah is Established by Choice, Not Inheritance
Al-Nasafi states that imamah is established by choice of the righteous, not inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that imamah is established through the choice of qualified community members, not by hereditary succession.

Core Idea
Imamah is a matter of community choice, not inheritance.

Al-Nasafi begins by addressing the question of how an imam is established. He contrasts two methods: selection by the righteous and inheritance. He aligns his view with the majority of scholars who accept Abu Bakr's imamah, and then introduces a dissenting group whose argument is cut off. This lesson clarifies the key principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the heading and the contrast between choice and inheritance.
The passage is concise; every word matters.
2
Identify the two methods
The passage presents two ways imamah could be established: by choice (اختيار) or by inheritance (وراثة). Notice which one the author affirms.
3
Understand the reference to Abu Bakr
Al-Nasafi says all scholars who affirm Abu Bakr's imamah hold this view. Reflect on why Abu Bakr is the reference point.
Abu Bakr's imamah was established by consensus (bay'ah), not heredity.
4
Consider the dissenting group
The author begins to mention the Rawandiyyah, who likely held that imamah is by inheritance. Think about what their argument might be.
The text cuts off, but the Rawandiyyah are a known sect.
5
Connect to the broader discussion
This passage sets the foundation for Maturidi political theology. Ask yourself why this distinction matters for the community's governance.
Imamah is a communal duty, not a family privilege.

بمن تثبت الإمامة ] ثم الإمامة عندنا تثبت باختيار أهل العدالة والصلاح لا بالوراثة. وإليه ذهب جميع من قال من علماء الأمة بصحة إمامة أبي بكر له. فأما الراوندية
[Section: By whom is imamah established?] Then imamah according to us is established by the choice of the people of justice and piety, not by inheritance. All the scholars of the community who affirm the validity of the imamah of Abu Bakr have held this view. As for the Rawandiyyah...
Source pages p. 1122

Commentary
This passage is a definition and statement of the Maturidi position on how the imam is established. The author begins with a heading asking 'By whom is imamah established?' Then he states the doctrine: imamah is established by the choice (اختيار) of the people of justice and piety, not by inheritance (وراثة). He notes that this is the view of all scholars who accept the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's imamah. Then he begins to mention a dissenting group, the Rawandiyyah, but the text cuts off. The Rawandiyyah were likely a group that held imamah by inheritance or something similar.

Refuting the Necessity of Imam's Infallibility
The author argues against the necessity of infallibility (عصمة) for the imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imam's infallibility is not a required condition according to Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
The imam is not infallible; he follows the same law as everyone else.

This passage challenges a common sectarian claim that the imam must be free from error. The author explains that the imam's role is simply to implement the revealed law, which is public knowledge. Therefore, requiring infallibility is unnecessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
Notice the author's direct refutation style.
2
Identify the main argument
Find the key point: the imams did not bring anything hidden; they only commanded acting on what the Prophet brought.
This sets the foundation for why infallibility is irrelevant.
3
Compare the imam to others
The author states the imam is like the rest of the community in acting according to the law. His correctness is judged by the same standards.
This directly undermines the need for infallibility.
4
Consider the author's earlier work
The author refers to his book against the Bāṭiniyya for a fuller treatment. This shows the depth of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الأئمة فما جاءوا بأمر غائب عن أهل الأرض بل هم أمروا بالعمل بما جاء به الرسول عليه السلام من القرآن وغيره، وذلك ظاهر فيما بين الناس، وقد قام بمعرفة ذلك كله علماء الأمة (وإنما الإمام للعمل بذلك والحكم به فيما بين الخلق وهو كسائر الأمة) في العمل بذلك يظهر صوابه وخطأه بما به يظهر صواب غيره وخطأه، فلا معنى لاشتراط عصمته، وقد بينا بطلان القول بعصمة الإمام في كتابنا المصنف في الرد على الباطنية المترجم بكتاب الإفساد لخدع أهل الإلحاد - بما فيه كفاية وفيما ذكرنا لها هنا مقنع.
As for the imams, they did not come with something hidden from the people of the earth; rather, they commanded to act according to what the Messenger, peace be upon him, brought from the Qur'an and other than it, and that is apparent among the people. The scholars of the community have undertaken the knowledge of all that. (The imam is only for acting according to that and judging by it among creation, and he is like the rest of the community) in acting according to that. His correctness and error become apparent by that by which the correctness and error of others become apparent. So there is no meaning to stipulating his infallibility (عصمته). And we have already shown the invalidity of the statement of the infallibility of the imam in our authored book refuting the Bāṭiniyya, titled Kitāb al-Ifsād li-Khudʿi Ahl al-Ilḥād, which contains sufficient proof, and what we have mentioned here is convincing.
Source pages p. 1122

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the imam must be infallible (maʿṣūm). The author argues that the imams (caliphs) did not bring any new hidden revelation; they merely commanded adherence to what the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم brought. Their rulings are based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, which are public. The scholars know these matters. The imam's role is to implement the law and judge among people, and in this he is like any other Muslim—his right and wrong are known just as anyone else's. Therefore, there is no need to stipulate his infallibility. The author further states he has already refuted this notion in detail in his book against the Bāṭiniyya, and what he mentions here suffices.

Key Terms
عصمة الإمام
الإمام
العمل بالشريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The imam must be infallible (maʿṣūm) to properly guide the community.
Correction: The imam is bound by the same public revelation as all Muslims, and his correctness is judged by the same standards; thus infallibility is not required.

Checkpoint

B) Because the imam's right and wrong are known the same way as others' right and wrong.
C) Because the imam is not required to follow the shari'a.
D) Because the imam brings new revelation.

Key Takeaway
The imam's authority does not require infallibility because his role is to apply the same revealed law that is known to all.

Imamate is Established by Choice, Not Inheritance
The author states the Sunni view and presents the Rawandiyya and Jarudiyya positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that imamate is established by the choice of upright people, and you will learn the views of three early sects (Rawandiyya and Jarudiyya) that claimed inheritance or textual designation.

Core Idea
Imamate is a matter of community choice, not bloodline.

The author begins by stating the orthodox Sunni view: imamate is not inherited but chosen by the community's upright members. He then introduces two deviant groups: the Rawandiyya, who claim al-ʿAbbas deserved it, and the Jarudiyya, who claim the Prophet designated ʿAlī by description and then it passed by inheritance. This lesson establishes the baseline and the heretical claims that will be refuted.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunni statement
Note the key term 'ikhtiyār' (choice) and that all scholars who affirm Abu Bakr's imamate agree on this.
2
Identify the Rawandiyya's two positions
They differ: some say inheritance, some say explicit text (nass).
3
Understand the Jarudiyya's unique claim
They hold that the Prophet designated ʿAlī by description, then inheritance with a condition of rising with a sword.
4
Notice the author's tone
He presents these views without refuting them yet; refutations come later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإمامة عندنا تثبت باختيار أهل العدالة والصلاح لا بالوراثة. وإليه ذهب جميع من قال من علماء الأمة بصحة إمامة أبي بكر له. فأما الراوندية القائلة بإمامة العباس وهم أتباع القاسم بن راوند فيختلفون فمنهم من زعم أن الإمامة تثبت بالوراثة وبها استحقها العباس [؟] الا الله، ومنهم من زعم أنه استحقها بنص النبي عليه السلام لا بالوراثة، وزعمت الجارودية من الروافض، وهم من جملة الزيدية أن النبي عليه السلام نص على خلافة علي رضي الله عنه بالوصف دون الاسم ثم ورثها من علي ابناه الحسن والحسين ثم إنهما على الميراث في هذين البطنين لا لواحد بعينه، ولكن من خرج منهم شاهرا سيفه يدعو إلى سبيل ربه وكان عالمًا صالحًا فهو الإمام، وزعم أكثر الإمامية أن الإمامة موروثة، وهذا خطأ، لأنها لو كانت بالوراثة لكان العباس أولى من علي رضي الله عنهما لأن العم أولى بالميراث من ابن العم وزعمهم أن عليا استحقه بالنص اضطرارًا لئلا يلزمهم هذا باطل، إذ لو كانت تستحق بالوراثة لما بطلت بالنص، ولا يحرم الوارث عن الميراث بنص الموروث أن الميراث لغيره، ثم لو كانت بالوراثة لما كان ينبغي أن يكون الحسن أولى بها من الحسين - رضي الله عنهما - ولما كان ينبغي أن ينتقل عن الحسن إلى الحسين مع وجود الأبناء للحسن ، ثم نبين بعد هذا إبطال ثبوت الخلافة بالنص وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافة الصديق يظهر بطلان القول بكونها مستحقة بالوراثة أو النص، والله الموفق.
Then, imamate according to us is established by the choice of the people of justice and righteousness, not by inheritance. All scholars of the community who affirm the validity of the imamate of Abu Bakr have held this. As for the Rawandiyya, who affirm the imamate of al-ʿAbbas and are followers of al-Qāsim ibn Rāwand, they differ: some of them hold that imamate is established by inheritance and thereby al-ʿAbbas deserved it [؟] except God, and some of them hold that he deserved it by a text (nass) of the Prophet, peace be upon him, not by inheritance. The Jarudiyya from the Rawāfiḍ, who are part of the Zaydiyya, claimed that the Prophet, peace be upon him, designated ʿAlī, may God be pleased with him, for the caliphate by description without naming, then it was inherited from ʿAlī by his two sons al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, and then it is inherited in these two lines, not for any one individual, but whoever among them comes out with his sword drawn calling to the way of his Lord and is knowledgeable and righteous, he is the imam. Most of the Imāmiyya hold that imamate is inherited, and this is wrong, because if it were by inheritance, then al-ʿAbbas would have been more entitled than ʿAlī, may God be pleased with them both, because the paternal uncle is more entitled to inheritance than the cousin. And their claim that ʿAlī deserved it by text out of necessity to avoid this objection is false, because if it were deserved by inheritance, it would not be nullified by text, and the heir cannot be deprived of inheritance by the text of the testator that the inheritance is for someone else. Moreover, if it were by inheritance, then al-Ḥasan should not have been more entitled to it than al-Ḥusayn, and it should not have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Then we will show after this the invalidity of establishing the caliphate by text and the occurrence of consensus on the caliphate of al-Ṣiddīq, which makes clear the falsehood of the claim that it is deserved by inheritance or text. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1122

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument establishing the Sunni view of imamate and refuting sectarian claims. The author first states the orthodox position: imamate is established by the choice (ikhtiyār) of upright people, not by inheritance. He notes that this is the view of all scholars who affirm Abu Bakr's imamate. Then he addresses three deviant groups: (1) The Rawandiyya, who claim al-ʿAbbas deserved imamate either by inheritance or by explicit text (nass) from the Prophet. (2) The Jarudiyya (a Zaydi subsect), who claim the Prophet designated ʿAlī by description, and then it passed by inheritance to his sons, with an additional condition that the imam must rise with a sword. (3) The Imāmiyya, who hold inheritance outright. The author refutes the inheritance claim: if it were hereditary, al-ʿAbbas (the Prophet's uncle) would be more entitled than ʿAlī (cousin). He points out that the Imāmiyya's resort to 'nass' to avoid this is invalid because inheritance cannot be overridden by a testator's text. He also argues that if it were inheritance, al-Ḥasan should not have been preferred over al-Ḥusayn, nor should it have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Finally, he promises to further prove the invalidity of nass and refer to consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Key Terms
إمامة
اختيار
وراثة
نص
راوندية
جارودية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some early sects believed imamate is inherited or based on a specific text from the Prophet.
Correction: The Sunni position holds that imamate is established by the choice of the community, not by bloodline or explicit designation.

Checkpoint
According to the Jarudiyya, what condition must an imam meet besides being from the Prophet's family?
A) He must be named explicitly by the Prophet.
B) He must draw his sword and call to God.
C) He must be the eldest son.
D) He must be chosen by the community.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that imamate is determined by community choice, not lineage or explicit divine text; deviant groups claimed otherwise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on your lineage or background to feel entitled to respect or authority, or do you strive to earn it through justice and righteousness? The Sunni view on imamate rejects inheritance—what does that mean for how you live your daily life?
?
The Jarudiyya required the imam to draw his sword and be knowledgeable and righteous. Are you prepared to take a stand for truth even when it's difficult? What one area of your life needs more courage or knowledge right now?
?
The Rawandiyya were divided—some chose inheritance, some chose text—to justify their preferred leader. Have you ever held onto a belief simply because it supported what you wanted to be true? How can you ensure your convictions are based on what is actually taught, not on personal bias?

Refuting Inheritance and Text in Imamate
The author refutes the Imamiyya inheritance claim and exposes logical inconsistencies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's logical refutations of the claims that imamate is hereditary or based on an explicit text (nass), focusing on the Imamiyya view and its inconsistencies.

Core Idea
If imamate were inherited, the Prophet's uncle would be more entitled, and inheritance rules would create contradictions.

After presenting the deviant views, the author now refutes the Imamiyya claim that imamate is hereditary. He shows that if it were inheritance, al-ʿAbbas would have been more entitled than ʿAlī, and the Imamiyya's resort to 'nass' is inconsistent because a testator's text cannot override inheritance law. He also points out that inheritance would make al-Ḥasan preferred over al-Ḥusayn, and it should not have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Finally, he promises to further demonstrate the invalidity of nass and appeal to consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Imamiyya claim
Most Imamiyya hold that imamate is inherited.
2
Analyze the first refutation
If inheritance, then al-ʿAbbas (uncle) is more entitled than ʿAlī (cousin) based on Islamic inheritance law.
3
Examine the second refutation
The Imamiyya's resort to nass is invalid because inheritance rules cannot be overridden by a testator's text.
4
Consider the third refutation
If inheritance, it should not pass from Hasan to Husayn while Hasan had sons.
5
Note the concluding promise
The author will further disprove nass and cite consensus on Abu Bakr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإمامة عندنا تثبت باختيار أهل العدالة والصلاح لا بالوراثة. وإليه ذهب جميع من قال من علماء الأمة بصحة إمامة أبي بكر له. فأما الراوندية القائلة بإمامة العباس وهم أتباع القاسم بن راوند فيختلفون فمنهم من زعم أن الإمامة تثبت بالوراثة وبها استحقها العباس [؟] الا الله، ومنهم من زعم أنه استحقها بنص النبي عليه السلام لا بالوراثة، وزعمت الجارودية من الروافض، وهم من جملة الزيدية أن النبي عليه السلام نص على خلافة علي رضي الله عنه بالوصف دون الاسم ثم ورثها من علي ابناه الحسن والحسين ثم إنهما على الميراث في هذين البطنين لا لواحد بعينه، ولكن من خرج منهم شاهرا سيفه يدعو إلى سبيل ربه وكان عالمًا صالحًا فهو الإمام، وزعم أكثر الإمامية أن الإمامة موروثة، وهذا خطأ، لأنها لو كانت بالوراثة لكان العباس أولى من علي رضي الله عنهما لأن العم أولى بالميراث من ابن العم وزعمهم أن عليا استحقه بالنص اضطرارًا لئلا يلزمهم هذا باطل، إذ لو كانت تستحق بالوراثة لما بطلت بالنص، ولا يحرم الوارث عن الميراث بنص الموروث أن الميراث لغيره، ثم لو كانت بالوراثة لما كان ينبغي أن يكون الحسن أولى بها من الحسين - رضي الله عنهما - ولما كان ينبغي أن ينتقل عن الحسن إلى الحسين مع وجود الأبناء للحسن ، ثم نبين بعد هذا إبطال ثبوت الخلافة بالنص وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافة الصديق يظهر بطلان القول بكونها مستحقة بالوراثة أو النص، والله الموفق.
Then, imamate according to us is established by the choice of the people of justice and righteousness, not by inheritance. All scholars of the community who affirm the validity of the imamate of Abu Bakr have held this. As for the Rawandiyya, who affirm the imamate of al-ʿAbbas and are followers of al-Qāsim ibn Rāwand, they differ: some of them hold that imamate is established by inheritance and thereby al-ʿAbbas deserved it [؟] except God, and some of them hold that he deserved it by a text (nass) of the Prophet, peace be upon him, not by inheritance. The Jarudiyya from the Rawāfiḍ, who are part of the Zaydiyya, claimed that the Prophet, peace be upon him, designated ʿAlī, may God be pleased with him, for the caliphate by description without naming, then it was inherited from ʿAlī by his two sons al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, and then it is inherited in these two lines, not for any one individual, but whoever among them comes out with his sword drawn calling to the way of his Lord and is knowledgeable and righteous, he is the imam. Most of the Imāmiyya hold that imamate is inherited, and this is wrong, because if it were by inheritance, then al-ʿAbbas would have been more entitled than ʿAlī, may God be pleased with them both, because the paternal uncle is more entitled to inheritance than the cousin. And their claim that ʿAlī deserved it by text out of necessity to avoid this objection is false, because if it were deserved by inheritance, it would not be nullified by text, and the heir cannot be deprived of inheritance by the text of the testator that the inheritance is for someone else. Moreover, if it were by inheritance, then al-Ḥasan should not have been more entitled to it than al-Ḥusayn, and it should not have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Then we will show after this the invalidity of establishing the caliphate by text and the occurrence of consensus on the caliphate of al-Ṣiddīq, which makes clear the falsehood of the claim that it is deserved by inheritance or text. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1122

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument establishing the Sunni view of imamate and refuting sectarian claims. The author first states the orthodox position: imamate is established by the choice (ikhtiyār) of upright people, not by inheritance. He notes that this is the view of all scholars who affirm Abu Bakr's imamate. Then he addresses three deviant groups: (1) The Rawandiyya, who claim al-ʿAbbas deserved imamate either by inheritance or by explicit text (nass) from the Prophet. (2) The Jarudiyya (a Zaydi subsect), who claim the Prophet designated ʿAlī by description, and then it passed by inheritance to his sons, with an additional condition that the imam must rise with a sword. (3) The Imāmiyya, who hold inheritance outright. The author refutes the inheritance claim: if it were hereditary, al-ʿAbbas (the Prophet's uncle) would be more entitled than ʿAlī (cousin). He points out that the Imāmiyya's resort to 'nass' to avoid this is invalid because inheritance cannot be overridden by a testator's text. He also argues that if it were inheritance, al-Ḥasan should not have been preferred over al-Ḥusayn, nor should it have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Finally, he promises to further prove the invalidity of nass and refer to consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Key Terms
إمامية
وراثة
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Shi'a believe imamate is inherited or based on a specific text from the Prophet, making it inviolable.
Correction: The author shows that both claims are logically flawed: inheritance would make al-ʿAbbas more entitled, and a text cannot override inheritance law.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say al-ʿAbbas is more entitled to imamate than ʿAlī if it were inheritance?
A) Because al-ʿAbbas was older.
B) Because the paternal uncle inherits before the cousin.
C) Because al-ʿAbbas was the Prophet's cousin.
D) Because ʿAlī was not a blood relative.

Key Takeaway
The claim that imamate is inherited or based on a text is logically inconsistent and contradicted by the consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This lesson shows that even a deeply held sectarian claim can be dismantled by simple logic. Are you willing to subject your own most cherished beliefs to the same scrutiny?
?
The Imamiyya claimed both inheritance and text, but the author shows they cannot coexist. Is there any area of your faith where you hold two contradictory positions without realizing it? What would it take for you to resolve that tension today?
?
The author uses a clear argument from Islamic inheritance law to refute a claim. When you encounter a claim about religion, do you test it against established principles from the Quran and Sunnah, or do you accept it because it comes from a respected source? How can you cultivate a habit of critical examination starting now?

Sectarian Views on Inheritance-Based Imamate
Nasafi lists two sects claiming inheritance-based imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different sectarian claims that imamate can be established by inheritance or designation, specifically the views of the Rawandiyya and the Jarūdiyya.

Core Idea
Sects differ: some say inheritance, some say designation.

Before refuting the claim that imamate is hereditary, Imam al-Nasafi surveys the views of various groups. This lesson introduces the Rawandiyya and the Jarūdiyya, two sects that each hold that the imamate passes through lineage, though they differ on the mechanism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups
Read the passage and note the two main groups mentioned: the Rawandiyya (followers of al-Qāsim ibn Rāwand) and the Jarūdiyya (a subsect of the Zaydiyya).
2
Understand the Rawandiyya’s internal disagreement
Notice that the Rawandiyya themselves are divided: some claim the imamate of al-‘Abbās is by inheritance, others by explicit designation (naṣṣ) from the Prophet.
This disagreement shows inconsistency even within the same sect.
3
Grasp the Jarūdiyya’s position
The Jarūdiyya claim that the Prophet designated ‘Alī by description (not by name), and then the imamate is inherited among the descendants of al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, with conditions of knowledge, righteousness, and armed rising.
They combine designation and inheritance in a unique way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القائلة بإمامة العباس وهم أتباع القاسم بن راوند فيختلفون فمنهم من زعم أن الإمامة تثبت بالوراثة وبها استحقها العباس، ومنهم من زعم أنه استحقها بنص النبي عليه السلام لا بالوراثة، وزعمت الجارودية من الروافض، وهم من جملة الزيدية أن النبي عليه السلام نص على خلافة علي بالوصف دون الاسم ثم ورثها من علي ابناه الحسن والحسين ثم إنهما على الميراث في هذين البطنين لا لواحد بعينه، ولكن من خرج منهم شاهرا سيفه يدعو إلى سبيل ربه وكان عالمًا صالحًا فهو الإمام، وزعم أكثر الإمامية أن الإمامة موروثة، وهذا خطأ، لأنها لو كانت بالوراثة لكان العباس أولى من علي رضي الله عنهما لأن العم أولى بالميراث من ابن العم وزعمهم أن عليا استحقه بالنص اضطرارًا لئلا يلزمهم هذا باطل، إذ لو كانت تستحق بالوراثة لما بطلت بالنص، ولا يحرم الوارث عن الميراث بنص الموروث أن الميراث لغيره، ثم لو كانت بالوراثة لما كان ينبغي أن يكون الحسن أولى بها من الحسين، ولما كان ينبغي أن ينتقل عن الحسن إلى الحسين مع وجود الأبناء للحسن، ثم نبين بعد هذا إبطال ثبوت الخلافة بالنص وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافة الصديق يظهر بطلان القول بكونها مستحقة بالوراثة أو النص، والله الموفق.
The group that affirms the imamate of al-‘Abbās, they are followers of al-Qāsim ibn Rāwand; they differ: some claim that imamate is established by inheritance and by it al-‘Abbās deserved it, and some claim that he deserved it by explicit designation (naṣṣ) from the Prophet, peace be upon him, not by inheritance. The Jārūdiyya of the Rāfiḍa, who are part of the Zaydiyya, claimed that the Prophet, peace be upon him, designated ‘Alī for the caliphate by description without naming, then his two sons al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn inherited it from ‘Alī; then the inheritance is in these two lines, not for one specific person, but whoever among them emerges drawing his sword calling to the way of his Lord, being knowledgeable and righteous, he is the imam. Most of the Imāmiyya claimed that imamate is inherited. This is wrong, because if it were by inheritance, then al-‘Abbās would be more entitled than ‘Alī, may Allah be pleased with them both, because the paternal uncle is more entitled to inheritance than the cousin. Their claim that ‘Alī deserved it by designation is out of necessity to avoid this [conclusion] being incumbent upon them; it is false, because if it were deserved by inheritance, it would not be invalidated by designation, nor does the designation of the testator that the inheritance is for someone else prevent the heir from inheritance. Also, if it were by inheritance, al-Ḥasan should not be more entitled than al-Ḥusayn, and it should not have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Then after this we will show the invalidation of the establishment of the caliphate by designation and the occurrence of consensus on the caliphate of al-Ṣiddīq, making clear the falsehood of the claim that it is deserved by inheritance or designation. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 1123

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that imamate is established by inheritance. The author begins by presenting the views of two groups: the Rawandiyya, who differ among themselves whether the imamate of al-‘Abbās is by inheritance or by explicit designation (naṣṣ), and the Jārūdiyya (a Zaydī sect) who hold that the Prophet designated ‘Alī by description, and that thereafter the imamate is inherited among the descendants of al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, with the condition that the imam be a learned, righteous person who rises with the sword. The majority of the Imāmiyya also claim inheritance. The author then declares this wrong and provides three arguments. First, if imamate were by inheritance, then al-‘Abbās (the Prophet’s uncle) would have a stronger claim than ‘Alī (the Prophet’s cousin), because in Islamic inheritance law the paternal uncle takes precedence over the cousin. To avoid this, the Rawandiyya claim that ‘Alī was designated by naṣṣ, but this is inconsistent: if the right were based on inheritance, the testator's designation cannot override it. Second, if inheritance were the basis, then al-Ḥasan would not be more entitled than his brother al-Ḥusayn (since both are sons of ‘Alī), nor should the imamate pass from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons (since sons are closer heirs). Third, the author announces that he will later prove the invalidity of naṣṣ altogether and the fact of consensus on Abū Bakr’s caliphate, which together refute both inheritance and designation. The passage follows the order: presentation of erroneous views, then logical refutation based on inheritance law, then a preview of further arguments.

Refutation of Inheritance and Designation
Nasafi refutes inheritance-based imamate with three logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi’s logical arguments against the claim that imamate is established by inheritance or exclusive designation, including the priority of the uncle over the cousin and inconsistencies in succession.

Core Idea
If imamate were inheritance, the uncle would precede the cousin.

After presenting the sectarian views, Imam al-Nasafi now provides clear logical refutations. He shows that if imamate were based on inheritance, it would contradict established Islamic inheritance laws and lead to absurd consequences. This lesson presents three key arguments and a preview of further proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Imāmiyya claim
Notice that most Imāmiyya are said to claim inheritance, which al-Nasafi calls wrong.
2
Examine the first argument: uncle vs. cousin
If imamate were by inheritance, al-‘Abbās (the uncle) would be more entitled than ‘Alī (the cousin) because Islamic inheritance law favors the paternal uncle over the cousin.
This argument relies on the standard rules of inheritance in Islam.
3
Understand the second argument: naṣṣ vs. inheritance
The Rawandiyya claim that ‘Alī was designated by naṣṣ to avoid the above conclusion. But al-Nasafi says if the right were based on inheritance, the testator’s designation cannot override it. Thus their position is inconsistent.
This shows that you cannot have both inheritance and designation as the basis.
4
Analyze the third argument: succession among descendants
If inheritance were the basis, al-Ḥasan should not be more entitled than al-Ḥusayn (since both are sons), and imamate should not pass from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. This would violate inheritance rules.
This argument highlights contradictions in the Jarūdiyya/Imāmiyya position.
5
Preview the final refutation
Al-Nasafi announces he will later prove that naṣṣ is invalid and that consensus (ijmā‘) established the caliphate of Abū Bakr, which together refute both inheritance and designation.
This prepares the reader for a broader proof beyond these logical arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Do you defend it, ignore it, or honestly re-examine? This lesson forces you to ask: are you willing to let evidence dismantle a cherished belief, even if it means changing your worldview?
?

Is that belief logically consistent with the principles you claim to accept? If not, what would it take for you to realign your belief with truth, even at the cost of personal pride?
?
The Imamiyya tried to combine inheritance and designation to support their claim, but Nasafi shows their position is internally inconsistent. Are there areas in your life where you hold two contradictory positions because both are comfortable or convenient? How can you actively seek to resolve that contradiction, starting today?

The Method of Ijtihad for the Imama
Introduction: method of imama and rejection of nass claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that, according to Imam al-Nasafi, the imama is established through ijtihad (independent reasoning), not through an explicit textual designation, and that the Shia claim of nass is baseless.

Core Idea
The imama is determined by ijtihad, just like other legal rulings.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by establishing the principle that the imama is determined through ijtihad (independent reasoning), not through an explicit textual designation. He then states that the Rafida and Rawandiyya claims of a nass for Ali or Abbas are false. This lesson introduces the foundational claim and sets up the refutation that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a very concise style here.
2
Identify the method for imama
The passage states that the imama is established 'by way of ijtihad and the use of opinion'. Contrast this with the claim of nass.
Ijtihad means independent reasoning, often used in deriving legal rulings.
3
Recognize the sects mentioned
The author refers to two groups: al-Rafida (Shia) and al-Rawandiyya. Note that their claims are dismissed as false.
This sets the stage for the detailed proof that follows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم طريق ثبوت الإمامة لمن يصلح أهلاً لها على سبيل الاجتهاد واستعمال الرأي على ما يستعمل في الحوادث الشرعية التي بالناس إلى معرفة أحكامها حاجة وقد عدموا فيها النص إذ لا نص ها هنا، وقول الروافض بوجود النص من النبي عليه السلام على علي عليه السلام وقول الراوندية بوجود النص على العباس باطل. رد القول بالنص في الإمامة والدليل على بطلان النص أن أمر الخلافة أمر عام يقع بكل الناس إلى معرفته حاجة ماسة، وما هذا سبيله كان النص فيه لو كان ثابتا يشتهر اشتهارا لا يبقى معه على أحد من الناس خفاء، ولا اضطر الناس إلى معرفته كالنص على القبلة وعلى أعداد ركعات الصلاة ومقاديرها وأوقاتها ومقادير النصيب والواجبات في باب الزكاة، وغير ذلك من الأمور العامة، ولما لم يوجد في ذلك خبر هذا سبيله، دل أن لا نص فيه البتة، يدل عليه أن النص لو كان ثابتا لما أعرضت الصحابة مع جلالة أقدارهم في الدين وشدة ورعهم وتمسكهم بالدين وتحرزهم عن مخالفة الشريعة عن قبوله والعمل به وتفويض الأمر إلى المنصوص عليه، بل بادروا إليه وولوه الأمر ولم ينازعه أحد في ذلك إذ لم يكن تقلد من تقلد للأمر منهم رغبة في الجاه والمنزلة والترأس ولا حرصا على جمع الحطام والاستمتاع باللذات البدنية والشهوات الطبيعية بل كان تقلدهم لذلك للقيام بحقوق الدين واستيفاء حقوق الله تعالى وتقوية الملة والسعى في إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى وقهر أعدائه وتشييد بنيان الإسلام ألا ترى الصديق الله كيف كانت معاملته الخلق ورفضه الشهوات والاكتفاء باليسير من القوت والخشن من الثياب والاجتزاء بقليل من بيت المال، ثم الأمر برد ذلك عند وفاته إلى بيت المال، وكذا عمره، وكذا الخليفتان بعدهما - رضي الله عنهما - وإذا كان تقلدهم لما ذكر فكيف يظن بواحد منهم الإعراض عن قبول النص الثابت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والتمسك بمخالفته؟! ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! ثم كيف امتنعوا عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن هذا المنكر الذي هو مخالفة رسول الله عليه السلام وغصب الأمر أهله، والقيام بتنفيذ الأحكام في الدماء والفروج والأموال من غير ثبوت الولاية مع أن الله تعالى وصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، ومدحهم على ذلك وأثنى به عليهم، أفترى الله تعالى لم يعلم بما يوجد منهم بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام من تقاعدهم عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، وتسارعهم إلى إعانة المبطل وخذلان المحق حتى وصفهم الله تعالى بذلك وأثنى عليهم به؟! وهذا والله هو الظن المحال والرأي الفاسد والقول الباطل. ثم كيف يظن مسلم أن رهط اختارهم الله تعالى لنصرة رسوله الذي هو خير البشر وصفوة الأنام وخيرته من خلقه، واصطفاهم لصحبته، وأسعدهم بقربه
Then the method of establishing the imama for one who is qualified for it is by way of ijtihad (independent reasoning) and the use of opinion, as is used in the religious incidents for which people have a need to know their rulings, and they have no text (nass) in them, for there is no text here. The statement of the Rafida that there is a nass from the Prophet, peace be upon him, for Ali, peace be upon him, and the statement of the Rawandiyya that there is a nass for al-Abbas, are false. Refutation of the claim of nass in the imama: The proof of the falsehood of the nass is that the matter of the caliphate is a general matter that concerns all people, and the need to know it is pressing. If it had been established by nass, it would have spread in such a way that no obscurity would remain for anyone, nor would people have been compelled to seek knowledge of it, like the nass on the qibla, the numbers of rak'ats of prayer, their measures and times, the shares and obligations in the chapter on zakat, and other general matters. Since no report of this kind has been found, it indicates that there is absolutely no nass in it. This is supported by the fact that if the nass had been established, the Companions, despite their great status in religion, their intense piety, their adherence to religion, and their caution against violating the Sharia, would not have turned away from accepting it and acting upon it and entrusting the matter to the designated person. Rather, they would have hastened to him and entrusted him with the affair, and no one would have disputed him in it, since those among them who assumed the matter did not do so out of desire for status, rank, or leadership, nor out of greed for collecting worldly goods or enjoying bodily pleasures and natural desires. Rather, their assumption was for the sake of fulfilling the rights of religion, executing the rights of Allah Almighty, strengthening the community (milla), striving to elevate the word of Allah Almighty, subduing His enemies, and reinforcing the structure of Islam. Do you not see how al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr) treated the people? He rejected pleasures, sufficed with the bare minimum of sustenance and coarse clothing, and contented himself with little from the treasury (bayt al-mal). Then he ordered that it be returned to the treasury at his death. Likewise Umar, and likewise the two caliphs after them—may Allah be pleased with them. If their assumption of power was as mentioned, how could it be thought of any of them that they would turn away from accepting a nass established from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and cling to opposing it? Even if one of them had strayed from his guidance, deviated from the right path, preferred opposing the Messenger, peace be upon him, and did not care about Allah’s wrath out of desire to amass worldly goods and increase in the forbidden, due to what he was innately disposed to of harshness and ill nature, how could the noble Companions, the leading Emigrants and Helpers, the scholars of the nation, and the best of the caliphs—whom Allah Almighty testified as being the best nation and made a middle nation to be witnesses over the people—have supported him in that? Then how could they have refrained from enjoining good and forbidding this evil, which is opposing the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and usurping the matter from its rightful people, and carrying out punishments concerning blood, private parts, and wealth without established authority, despite the fact that Allah Almighty described them with enjoining good and forbidding evil, praised them for it, and commended them? Do you suppose that Allah Almighty did not know what would occur from them after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of their falling short in enjoining good and forbidding evil, and their hastening to support the wrongdoer and abandon the truth, such that He described them with that and praised them for it? This, by Allah, is impossible speculation, corrupt opinion, and false statement. Then how can a Muslim think that a group whom Allah Almighty chose to support His Messenger, who is the best of mankind, the elite of people, and His chosen among His creation, and whom He selected for his companionship and blessed with proximity to him...
Source pages p. 1124

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shia claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali (or for the Rawandiyya, al-Abbas) as his successor. The author gives a multi-step proof. First, he establishes that the imama is determined by ijtihad, not by nass, since there is no textual designation. He then provides the main proof: if such a nass existed, it would be as widely known as other public matters like the direction of prayer or the number of rak'ats, because the caliphate concerns everyone. The absence of such widespread transmission proves no nass exists. Second, he argues that the Companions were too pious and righteous to ignore a clear command from the Prophet. They assumed leadership not for worldly gain but to serve the religion, as shown by Abu Bakr and Umar's austerity. Third, even if one Companion had deviated, the rest of the pious Companions would have objected and enjoined good, but they unanimously accepted the caliphate of Abu Bakr. Finally, he concludes with a rhetorical question: how can a Muslim believe that Allah would praise the Companions as the best nation if they were to support a usurper? The entire argument is structured as a logical and theological refutation, using the character of the Companions as evidence.

Key Terms
نص
إمامة
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, how is the imama established?
A) By explicit textual designation (nass) from the Prophet
B) By ijtihad and the use of opinion
C) By consensus of the companions
D) By hereditary succession

Key Takeaway
The imama is a matter of ijtihad, not nass; the Shia claim of a text for Ali is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that something in your faith must be explicitly commanded in the Quran or hadith to be valid, and if so, how does that assumption affect your trust in the community's collective reasoning? Reflect on the concept of ijtihad: What matters in your life today could benefit from sound reasoning rather than waiting for a clear text? Commit to one area where you will practice ijtihad (seeking knowledge and making a decision) rather than demanding a nass.
?
This lesson teaches that the imama is not decided by divine text but by qualified individuals using ijtihad. Do you secretly wish for a leader who is supernaturally appointed, so you don't have to bear the responsibility of evaluating and choosing? Examine your heart: Are you avoiding the duty of discernment in communal matters by passively hoping for a 'savior'? Resolve to study the qualities of a just leader and actively participate in your community's decision-making, however small.
?
The author dismisses the claims of nass for Ali and al-Abbas as false. Have you ever clung to a belief about leadership or sect without examining whether it is based on a text or on speculation? Are you willing to accept that some important matters are left for human reasoning, or do you find that uncomfortable? Pray for the humility to recognize where Allah has not given explicit guidance and to trust the collective ijtihad of the Ummah.

Proof of Nass: Necessity of Widespread Knowledge
Main proof: absence of widespread knowledge indicates no nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key argument that if a nass had existed, it would have been as widely known as other public rulings, and its absence proves no nass exists.

Core Idea
A divine text on the caliphate would be universally known; its absence disproves the claim.

Imam al-Nasafi presents the central proof: the caliphate is a general matter, so any nass would be as famous as the rulings on prayer and zakat. Since no such widespread report exists, the claim of nass is baseless.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical structure: premise, analogy, conclusion.
The author uses a comparison with well-known religious rulings.
2
Note the comparison to other nass rulings
The author compares the hypothetical nass on the caliphate to the nass on the qibla, rak'ats, and zakat obligations. These are universally known.
If the caliphate nass existed, it would be equally famous.
3
Understand the logical implication
Since no such widespread report is found, the logical conclusion is that no nass exists.
This is a powerful argument from absence of expected evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The proof here relies on what is publicly and universally known. Are there areas of your faith where you rely on hidden or exclusive knowledge? Could that be a sign of a weak foundation? Commit today to seeking knowledge that is clear and widespread, and avoid claims that are obscure.

The Character of the Companions as Evidence
Argument from Companions' piety and unanimous acceptance of Abu Bakr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the piety and actions of the Companions, especially Abu Bakr and Umar, prove that no nass existed, as they would not have ignored a clear command.

Core Idea
The Companions' piety and unanimous acceptance of Abu Bakr's caliphate disprove any hidden nass.

Imam al-Nasafi uses the exemplary character of the Companions as evidence. If there had been a nass, they would have followed it without hesitation. He highlights the austerity of Abu Bakr and Umar to show they had no worldly motives. He then argues that even if one had deviated, the others would have corrected him. Finally, he concludes with a rhetorical question about Allah's praise of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument about the Companions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the multiple sub-arguments: the Companions' piety, their actual behavior, and the hypothetical scenario.
The author uses the Companions' known character as evidence.
2
Note the description of Abu Bakr's piety
The author describes Abu Bakr's austerity and lack of worldly ambition. This shows that the Companions had no motive to ignore a nass.
Similar description is given for Umar and the later caliphs.
3
Understand the hypothetical scenario and conclusion
Even if one Companion had deviated, the others would have objected due to their duty to enjoin good. The fact that they accepted Abu Bakr unanimously proves no nass existed.
The author ends with a rhetorical question about Allah's praise of the Companions.
