Ali's Inaction Refutes the Claim of Nass
The author argues that Ali's failure to fight disproves the Rafidah claim of an explicit text (nass).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Ali's inaction to refute the claim of explicit text (nass) and the theological implications of the Rafidah position.

Core Idea
Ali's failure to fight disproves the claim of a divine text designating him as immediate successor.

This passage is a polemical argument against those who claim an explicit text (nass) designating Ali as the immediate successor. The author presents a practical argument: if Ali had such a mandate, he would have acted on it, but he didn't, so there is no nass. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the stakes involved.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two parts
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice that the argument has two main parts: Ali's inaction proves no nass, and the Rafidah claim leads to slander.
2
Understand the argument from inaction
The author argues that if Ali had a nass, he would have fought for his right, especially in the early period when Companions were most supportive. His inaction shows he knew there was no nass.
Consider why the early period is emphasized.
3
Reflect on the implications of the Rafidah claim
The author contends that claiming nass for Ali forces one to accuse Ali of cowardice and Allah of choosing corrupt Companions. Recognize the theological stakes.
This shows the argument is not just about history but about divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تولى الأمر بعده بتقليده ولا زوجه بنته وهو ظالم عليه بغصبه حقه وعاص الله تعالى بالإعراض عن نص رسوله عليه السلام بل هو كافر على رأي الغلاة منهم مع العلم أنه لو لم يرض بالذل والقهر وشهر سيفه وطلب في ذات الله تعالى حقه لم يعدم من أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام أنصارًا وأعوانًا كما لم يعدم عند طلبه حقه وقت خلافته بل كان ذلك في أول الأمر كان أحق وأولى إذ كان عهد رسول الله عليه السلام أقرب وزمانه أدنى والصحابة كانوا وقتئذ أرق أفئدة وأرغب في اتباع الهدى وأزهد فيما يخالف الدين وسنة الرسول عليه السلام وأميل إلى نصرة الحق وخذلان الباطل. وحيث لم يجرد سيفه ولم يطلب حقه والحال في نفسه والصحابة ما وصف دل أنه لم يفعل ذلك لأنه علم أن لا نص له ولا لغيره، وأن من قلدته الصحابة ورضيت بإمامته كان أولى به منه ومن غيره. فالروافض بما ادعوا من النص صاروا طاعنين على الصحابة على العموم وعلى علي على الخصوص حيث وصفوه بالجبن والضعف، وقلة التوكل على الله تعالى في نصرة المحق وخذلان المبطل، وعدم الثقة بوعد الرسول المفوض إليه الأمر الناص عليه بذلك والخنوثة حين زوج بنته من هو قاهره ومستذله وغاصبه حقه خوفًا من معرته ورضي بأن يستولي على ابنته من هو عاص أو كافر لينال هو السلامة، وهذه درجة لا يرضى بها لنفسه من هو أخس خليقة الله وأرذلهم نفسا ونسبًا. ثم صاروا واصفين الله تعالى بالكذب والخطأ في التدبير حيث وصف مثل هؤلاء الصحابة مع علمه بما يصنعون بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من تقوية المبطل واختارهم لصحبة صفيه ونجيبه - لعن الله من هذا قوله في الله ورسوله والمنتخبين من الخلق لصحبه ورسوله.
He took charge of the matter after him by his appointment and did not marry his daughter to him, and he is an oppressor for usurping his right and disobedient to Allah by turning away from the text of His Messenger, peace be upon him, rather he is a disbeliever according to the view of the extremists among them, despite the knowledge that if he had not accepted humiliation and subjugation and had unsheathed his sword and sought his right for the sake of Allah, he would not have lacked supporters and helpers from among the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, just as he did not lack when he sought his right at the time of his caliphate. Rather, that was in the beginning most appropriate and prior, for the era of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was nearer and his time closer, and at that time the Companions were more tender-hearted, more desirous of following guidance, more ascetic in what opposed the religion and the Sunnah of the Messenger, peace be upon him, and more inclined to supporting truth and abandoning falsehood. Since he did not unsheathe his sword and did not seek his right, while his state and that of the Companions was as described, it indicates that he did not do so because he knew that there was no text (nass) for him or for anyone else, and that the one whom the Companions appointed and were pleased with his leadership was more entitled to it than him and than others. So the Rafidah (Rawafid), by their claim of a text (nass), have become criticizers of the Companions in general and of ‘Ali in particular, as they have described him as cowardice, weakness, lack of trust in Allah in supporting the truth and abandoning falsehood, lack of confidence in the promise of the Messenger to whom the matter was delegated and who gave the text about him, and effeminacy (khunutha) when he married his daughter to one who overpowered him, humiliated him, and usurped his right, fearing his harm, and he was pleased that someone who is a sinner or disbeliever should take control of his daughter so that he might attain safety. This is a rank that not even the basest of Allah’s creation and the most contemptible in soul and lineage would be pleased with for himself. Then they became describers of Allah Almighty with falsehood and error in administration, as He described such Companions (knowing what they would do after the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, of strengthening the false) and chose them for the companionship of His chosen and intimate friend – may Allah curse the one who says this concerning Allah, His Messenger, and the chosen ones from among creation for the companionship of His Messenger.
Source pages p. 1128

Commentary
This passage is a polemical refutation of the Rafidah (Shi'a) claim that there was an explicit text (nass) designating 'Ali as the immediate successor of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author presents a two-part argument based on 'Ali's own conduct. First, the author argues that if 'Ali had truly possessed such a divine mandate (nass), he would have unsheathed his sword and fought for his right, especially during the early period when the Companions were most receptive to truth and justice. 'Ali's failure to do so proves he knew there was no nass for him or anyone else, and that the Caliph chosen by the Companions was the rightful leader. Second, the author contends that the Rafidah's claim of nass necessarily implies slander against 'Ali himself, accusing him of cowardice, weakness, and lack of trust in Allah, as well as against Allah, who allegedly chose corrupt Companions despite foreknowledge of their actions. The passage uses strong language to condemn this position.

Key Terms
نص (nass)
روافض (Rawafid)
صحابة (Companions)
علي (Ali)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument is about 'Ali's personal courage or fear of the Companions.
Correction: The argument is theological: 'Ali's inaction shows he lacked a divine mandate (nass), not that he was afraid.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does 'Ali's failure to unsheathe his sword and demand his right indicate?
A) That he was too weak to fight.
B) That he knew he had no explicit text (nass).
C) That he feared the Companions.
D) That he was not interested in leadership.

Key Takeaway
The absence of a fight from Ali undermines the claim of textual designation, and the Rafidah claim leads to slander of Ali and Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a claim about someone's authority or status without examining whether their actions align with that claim? What belief are you holding today based on assumption rather than evidence, and are you willing to test it against reality?
?
If you truly believed someone was wrongfully deprived of their right, would you act? What does your own inaction in the face of injustice say about your convictions and trust in Allah's support?
?
The Rafidah claim leads to accusing Allah of error and the Companions of corruption. Have you ever held a belief that, if followed to its logical conclusion, would slander Allah or His chosen ones? Are you ready to re-examine your inherited beliefs to ensure they honor Allah and His Messenger?

Reductio ad Absurdum Against the Rafidah Claim of Nass
Refutation of the Rafidah claim of nass via reductio and authenticity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a reductio ad absurdum and an authenticity argument to refute the Rafidah claim of an explicit text (nass) for 'Ali's caliphate.

Core Idea
The claim of nass collapses under its own absurdity and lack of authentic transmission.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of the Rafidah (Shi'a) claim that there was an explicit divine text (nass) designating 'Ali as the caliph. The author employs a reductio ad absurdum: if the Companions could ignore such a nass, then one could claim they also ignored all core worship obligations, which would nullify Islam. He then counters potential objections about the authenticity of contradictory historical reports, demonstrating that the claimed nass lacks widespread transmission and contradicts the consensus of the Ummah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the reductio argument
Read the first part of the passage where the author poses a hypothetical: if ignoring a nass is permissible, then why not claim the Companions ignored all pillars of Islam? This shows the absurdity of the Rafidah position.
The author forces the opponent to either distinguish their case or accept the destruction of the religion.
2
Examine the response to authenticity objections
The passage then anticipates the objection that the mentioned historical reports (e.g., 'Ali marrying his daughter to 'Umar) are not authentic. The author contrasts their widespread transmission and use in legal rulings with the unknown nature of the claimed nass.
Notice how the author uses examples familiar to the reader to show the inconsistency.
3
Grasp the final conclusion
The author concludes that the claimed nass contradicts consensus, lacks transmission by reliable narrators, and implies denying Allah and slandering 'Ali.
This seals the argument by showing the harmful consequences of the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: لو جاز الإعراض عن مثل هذا النص الوارد في مثل هذه الحادثة التي تعم بها البلوى، فما تنكرون على من زعم أن الله تعالى نسخ هذه الصلوات والحج والزكاة وصوم شهر رمضان وفرض مكانها عبادات أُخر إلا أن الصحابة أعرضوا عن قبولها وأجمعوا على ترك العمل بها أفيصح قول هذا الزعم؟ فإن قالوا: لا - طولبوا بالفرق بين هذا وبين ما يدعون. وإن قالوا: نعم يصح هذا فقد أبطلوا الدين ورفضوا الشرائع، ولم يبق دليل أن هذه الشريعة شريعة الرسول عليه السلام وأن هذا الدين دينه، وهو أقوى طرق الإلحاد، وأوضح سبل هذا العناد - عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك ولقد صدق من قال: أروّض رافضيا لي صغيرا - أريكم منه زنديقا كبيرا ولو زعموا أن ما ذكرتم من تزويجه بنته من عمر الله وما ذكرتم من مخاطبته إياهم بالخلافة وأمره المؤمنين وغير ذلك، ليس بثابت، قلنا: لو لم تثبت هذه الأحاديث مع اشتهارها وتداول أيدي النقلة إياها وتدوين أهل الأخبار إياها في المصنفات، واحتجاج أهل الفقه بنقل علي الله ابنته أم كلثوم من دار عمر الله بعد ما قتل إلى دار نفسه في جواز اعتداد المتوفى عنها زوجها في غير بيت زوجها عند تعذر الاعتداد في بيت زوجها كيف تثبت روايتكم النص على عليه؟ وهذا ما انعقد إجماع الأمة بخلافه، ولم يشتهر عند النقلة ولا رواه أحد من الأئمة حملة الآثار، ثم فيه ما فيه من تكذيب الله تعالى والطعن على علي الله عليه
Then it is said to them: If turning away from such a text (nass) that occurred concerning such an incident of general affliction is permissible, then what do you say against the one who claims that Allah Almighty abrogated these prayers, Hajj, Zakat, and fasting of Ramadan and prescribed other acts of worship instead, except that the Companions turned away from accepting them and unanimously agreed to abandon acting upon them? Is such a statement correct? If they say: No – they are asked to differentiate between this and what they claim. If they say: Yes, this is correct – then they have nullified the religion and rejected the laws, and no proof remains that this Shariah is the Shariah of the Messenger, peace be upon him, and that this religion is his religion. This is the strongest way of heresy and the clearest path of obstinacy. May Allah protect us from that. And truthful is he who said: 'I train a young Rafidi — I show you from him a great zindiq.' Even if they claim that what you mentioned – of his marrying his daughter to ‘Umar, and what you mentioned of his addressing them with the caliphate and his commanding the believers, etc. – is not established, we say: If these hadiths are not established, despite their widespread fame, the transmission chains of narrators, and the recording of traditionists in compilations, and the jurists’ use of the transmission that ‘Ali moved his daughter Umm Kulthum from the house of ‘Umar after he was killed to his own house to infer the permissibility of a widow’s ‘idda in a house other than her husband’s house when it is impossible to observe the ‘idda in her husband’s house, then how can your narration of the text (nass) for ‘Ali be established? This is something upon which the consensus of the Ummah is contrary, and it is not widely known among the transmitters, nor has any of the imams who bear traditions narrated it. Moreover, it contains what it contains of denying Allah and slandering ‘Ali.
Source pages p. 1129

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the Rafidah (Shi'a) claim of an explicit text (nass) for 'Ali's caliphate. The author employs two main arguments. First, a reductio ad absurdum: if it were permissible to ignore a divinely mandated text in such a widely-affecting matter as the succession, then one could equally claim that the Companions ignored all the pillars of Islam (prayer, Hajj, fasting, etc.) and that these were abrogated. If the Rafidah reject this absurdity, they must explain why ignoring the supposed nass is different. If they accept it, their position destroys the entire religion. Second, the author addresses the objection that the hadiths about 'Ali marrying his daughter to 'Umar and other historical reports are not authentic. The author counters that these hadiths are widely transmitted, recorded in authoritative collections, and even used by jurists for legal rulings (like the 'idda of a widow). In contrast, the Rafidah's narration of nass lacks widespread transmission, contradicts the consensus of the Ummah, and was not narrated by any reliable traditionist. Hence, the claimed nass is false, and maintaining it leads to denial of Allah and slander of 'Ali.

Key Terms
نص (nass)
إجماع (consensus)
حديث (hadith)
زنديق (zindiq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is simply attacking the Rafidah without logical reasoning.
Correction: The author systematically uses reductio ad absurdum and historical authenticity arguments to refute the claim of nass. His reasoning is methodical and based on established scholarly principles.

Checkpoint
What is the reductio ad absurdum argument used by the author against the Rafidah?
A) If ignoring a nass is allowed, one could claim the Companions ignored all pillars of Islam.
B) If the hadiths are authentic, then the nass must be true.
C) Ali's marriage to his daughter proves the nass.
D) The Rafidah are disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
The claimed nass for 'Ali is logically absurd and historically unsubstantiated; maintaining it leads to heresy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author warns that accepting the Rafidah claim could lead to the nullification of the entire religion. Reflect: Are there any beliefs you hold that, if logically extended, would require you to reject well-established truths of Islam? What would it take for you to abandon such beliefs?
?
The author uses the marriage of 'Ali's daughter to 'Umar as a widely known historical fact. Is there a historical or religious fact that you have avoided accepting because it conflicts with your sectarian attachments? How will you reconcile your loyalty to truth with your loyalty to your group?
?
Consider the Rafidah's failure to provide authentic transmission for their claim. Are you always rigorous in verifying the sources of your religious knowledge, or do you sometimes accept claims based on emotional appeal or association? Commit to one concrete step to improve your critical engagement with Islamic sources this week.
